Merchants from Northern Jiangsu Present a Document to the Authorities Regarding the Reorganization of Salt Affairs Agencies 131

Salt merchants Wang Jianqiu, Tang Xinan, Wu Xiuzheng, Liu Zhuting, Qiao Shuangqiu, Kang Shuwen, Qiu Yuzhou, Zhu Yabo, Yuan Yuetan, Wang Mingxiao, Xu Xiangjiu, and Li Yangren, et al., from Northern Jiangsu, presented a document to the financial and salt affairs authorities regarding the reorganization of salt affairs agencies. The original text is recorded as follows: Presenting [this document] for the auditing concurrently holding positions, outstanding achievements, merchants feeling convinced, looking up to and requesting the approval of public opinion, in order to promote justice, and avoid confusion of black and white. We humbly believe that in times of national crisis and financial difficulties, simplification of government is the priority. The key to simplifying government is to simplify officials. More agencies mean more waste, and even more opportunities for corruption. Under the old system of Chinese salt affairs, administration, anti-smuggling, and auditing were governed separately, without mutual leadership. When an administrative official performed an official duty, he had to consult with the auditors. When an auditor caught a salt smuggler, he had to send a letter to the anti-smuggling agency for handling. For ordinary matters, there was not much difference. In special cases, there were conflicts of interest. Not only were official documents delayed, but also conflicting opinions were generated, and the harm was unimaginable. Moreover, many administrative personnel were corrupt, and the anti-smuggling bureaus were even more deeply flawed. Therefore, in the 20th year of the Republic of China, the financial officer believed that various salt affairs agencies were subordinate to the Ministry of Finance. In addition to auditing, they were all superfluous agencies. He specially requested the approval of the Executive Yuan to appoint the director-general of the General Office of Salt Affairs Auditing concurrently as the director of the Salt Affairs Department, and to appoint the auditors of the auditing offices of Xiang, E, Western Anhui, and each bank concurrently as the directors of the Transportation Bureaus of each bank. The managers of the auditing sub-offices of Shandong, Fujian, Zhejiang, and Northern Jiangsu were concurrently appointed as the commissioners of each region, and the managers of the auditing sub-offices of Songjiang and Southern Jiangsu were concurrently appointed as the deputy commissioners of the region. Foreign auditors of each region still held their original positions. All anti-smuggling and administrative matters were handled concurrently by Chinese officials. Since the auditing concurrently holding positions in the 20th year of the Republic of China, the national income has increased by 76 million yuan compared with the 10th year of the Republic of China. The expenditure item can save 3 million yuan per year, and the elimination of malpractices has reached 700,000 to 800,000 yuan. Taking Zhejiang as an example, since auditing concurrently holding positions, the tax revenue in 20 years and 9 months has increased to 400,000 yuan. After the cancellation of the Wenzhou contractor, the tax revenue has been consolidated to more than 100,000 yuan. The tax police expenses can be saved by more than 100,000 yuan. Taking Northern Jiangsu as an example, since the auditing concurrently holding positions, the tax revenue in the 20th year was 11,545,000 yuan, the tax revenue in the 21st year has reached 12,447,000 yuan, and by the 22nd year, it has increased to 17 million yuan by the end of October, and to more than 20 million yuan by the end of December, which is an unprecedented achievement. As for saving expenses and eliminating black fees, it is only a small matter of tens of thousands of dollars. All the above-mentioned are based on reliable evidence, and are by no means empty words and embellishments, so they can be compared to flattering words. Unless those who rely on malpractices for food and have the intention of holding grudges and sabotage, everyone has a good reputation. However, this is only in terms of finance. Let us analyze it again from the facts that can be called commendable. First, construction: It can be seen that several years ago, there was no direct road for cars from Banpu Yunshe to Yanzhen, there were no tax police distributed, and there was no salt pile as a place to return. Bandits were rampant, salt beaches were abandoned, and merchants suffered from it. Since the auditing concurrently holding positions, car roads are like chessboard, tax police teams are standing tall, and there are salt piles as a place to return. There are telephones in the salt pile, and they can travel back and forth in one day. Anti-smuggling and bandit suppression are convenient. The rivers transporting salt have been dredged for about 100 miles to facilitate transportation and many sluice gates have been built to save water. Self-running water wells have been added in places without drinking water to ensure hygiene. Yanzhen can be called a paradise. The price of salt ponds has increased, and the people of the place whose rural areas are bankrupt and lying on pillows are no less than the difference between heaven and earth compared with the fact that no one has cared about the salt ponds for several years and they have almost stopped operating. This is the merit of construction. Second, anti-smuggling: It can be seen that before anti-smuggling was merged, the anti-smuggling army was named anti-smuggling, but in fact it was releasing smuggling. Smuggled salt spread all over the place. The annual tax revenue was only 10 million yuan, or only 7 to 8 million yuan, or 5 to 6 million yuan. Except for special accidents in the 19th year, the tax revenue increased sharply, and the malpractice of over-sales and backlog was still not eliminated. Since the auditing concurrently holding positions in the 20th year, not only is the regular amount sold smoothly, but also the amount that has not been sold in Jinan for six years will be replenished in the 22nd year in order to enrich the national tax. In the past, people in the five counties and five counties ate coastal salt, but in recent years, official salt shops have been set up in various counties, and the average tax rate is not restricted. Even those who make salt do not eat untaxed salt. There have been people who have applied for an increase in the amount of sales because the amount of sales is too small every month. This shows that there is more official salt and less smuggled salt. The more official salt there is, the smoother the sales market is, and the smoother the sales market is, the higher the tax rate will be. This is a natural cycle. In the past, places such as Tanggou in Shuyang, Linhong in Donghai, Qingsantuan in Ganyu, and various seaports in Guan, Lian, Fu, and Ning were all important ways to smuggle. In recent years, the malpractices have been eliminated and the atmosphere has been cleared. Why are the roads for smuggled salt cut off? It is the merit of anti-smuggling. Third, bandit suppression: In the past, bandits and salt bandits were divided, and anti-smuggling and bandit suppression were also divided. In recent years, bandits and salt bandits have merged, and anti-smuggling and bandit suppression have to merge. In the past, the anti-smuggling camp was often disarmed by bandits in the Longju Dongzhuo Mountain area, and camp officials were also killed from time to time. Therefore, the Yanzhen area was mostly occupied by bandits, and it was common to lift people and rob them. Since the tax police were merged into auditing in the 20th year, Yangji, Wangji, Yaoyu in Guanyun, Longju, Xinba in Donghai, and various borders in Shu, Gan, Lian, and Fu occupied by bandits were all bravely repelled by the tax police, killing and injuring countless people. There are reports on file. All of the above are places far away from the salt beach that rely on the tax police for protection, and why there are no bandits in Taiping, Zhongfu, Linxing, and Jinan Yanzhen? It is the merit of bandit suppression. Fourth, the unification of power: There is no lack of talent in administrative anti-smuggling. In fact, the legislation is not good, people have no guarantee. When the country is in trouble, it cannot fully enforce the law. Therefore, everyone has the intention of being a magistrate for five days. The act of theft is almost like the Yin people will eat without disaster. Even the dignity of the deputy commissioner is only used to entangle matters and has already been wanted. Even the weight of the director is now escaped because of the tax guarantee relationship. The past is not forgotten, and the future is a teacher. It is impossible not to observe it. Since the auditing concurrently holding positions, there is no matter of exercise and accommodation in the administrative process. The anti-smuggling matters are as easy as an arm to use, and there is no suspicion of being too big to fall. Because of this concurrent position, it can resist the interference of foreign troops from the outside, and there is no fear of slanderous books from the inside. It is up to the authorities to trust it from beginning to end. The four items presented above refer to the outstanding ones. They are all achievements after the concurrent positions. If there is no public opinion as a backing, it will inevitably lead to the destruction of public opinion and the accumulation of destruction by those who hold grudges. It is in embellished rhetoric, either saying that sovereignty is lost and handed over to foreigners, or that auditing is arbitrary and abuses its power. If it is said that sovereignty is lost, the country does not have an explicit order for foreign auditors, and foreign auditors have not interfered with the act of concurrently holding positions. If it is said to be arbitrary, it should also examine the facts and not listen to one-sided unfounded words, and then decide on the case of Zeng Shen killing people. For the sake of the overall situation, Jianqiu and others dare not avoid suspicion and resentment, and explain everything in detail. We humbly ask for your approval of public opinion in order to promote justice and avoid confusion between black and white, which is a public convenience.

The Ministry of Communications Orders Shipping Companies in Shanghai to Vigorously Improve Ship Management and Reform the Malpractices of the Business Department 132

Our country's ship management has never had a fixed system, and the number of crew members has never been stipulated. The comprador system of the business department and the tea room system of various cabin classes are the worst habits. The improvement of ship management proposed by the last Promotion of Shipping Conference has been decided by the Ministry of Communications to unify the crew system of sea-going ships and river ships (already recorded in the 20th issue of this newspaper, omitted) and to eliminate the bad habits of the business department, vigorously implement the new system, abolish the comprador, prohibit tea room extortion, improve ship facilities, and rectify pier management. Yesterday, the Ministry of Communications issued an order to the shipping companies in Shanghai to vigorously implement the formulated measures. The following is a summary of its general outline:

Abolish the Comprador and Change to Administrators. In other countries, business management on ships does not use the comprador system, only our country has this abnormal system. When foreign ships first sailed in the mainland of our country, they were not familiar with business, so they hired Chinese people as compradors. This has been going on until today, and domestic merchant ships also have a comprador position, and the system of charging passengers and packages is used, resulting in many malpractices. Compradors only seek to increase their income. Sometimes passengers exceed the limit, causing danger. Last year, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company implemented the abolition of the comprador system, but only two or three ships, such as the Pu'an and Xinming, broke this long-standing habit. Now, the Ministry of Communications has decided to abolish all ship compradors. The duties of the business department will be assumed by administrators who are hired by the shipping companies and are familiar with shipping matters in order to break the system of charging passengers and packages.

Revolutionize the Bad Habits of Tea Rooms. For the servants and tea rooms needed on the ship, the shipping company shall hire polite tea rooms, train them, and pay them monthly wages. They are responsible for taking care of the passengers on the ship. The various bad habits of the tea rooms used on the original ships must be thoroughly eliminated, and the number of tea rooms must be stipulated. They are not allowed to solicit alcohol and other expenses from passengers at will. If there is any of the above, the passengers may report to the administrator, who will immediately dismiss and replace them. After the various ships are inspected and determined by the Shipping Administration Bureau, passengers must abide by the specified number. The number of passengers in the economy class must not exceed the limit in order to prevent a major danger from occurring. Pay Attention to Various Facilities. Ship hygiene and cleanliness are not valued by the current ships. It is now limited to ships from 200 tons and above, and the voyage starts from one day to arrival. One to two doctors should be added to the ship to diagnose the passengers' illnesses. Various classes of cabins should pay more attention to hygiene and cleanliness. Isolation rooms should also be set up on the ship so that in case there are passengers with infectious diseases, they can be moved to the isolation room to avoid danger to the public. In addition, ships should depart at a fixed time and should not be delayed at will. As for the piers, marine police should be equipped, and passengers should be strictly guarded when boarding and disembarking and loading and unloading goods, and hoodlums should be driven away.

Dutch East Indies Government Formulates Regulations on Firecrackers and Fireworks, Chinese Merchants Pay Attention 133

The Central News Agency reported that according to Li Zejin, director of the Guidance Department of the International Trade Bureau, our country's firecrackers and fireworks are well-made, and are frequently exported, especially to Southeast Asia. In recent years, the Dutch East Indies has also set up factories to manufacture them, with a total of 31 factories, but the products are immature and the quantity is limited. The average annual value is about 1.35 million guilders, while the average annual consumption of firecrackers and fireworks in the Dutch East Indies is about 6 million guilders, of which 91% are sounding firecrackers, especially firecrackers. 19 of these firecrackers are imported from our country.

Motivation for Formulating Regulations 134

The local factories also have considerable achievements, so the establishment of these regulations is to protect the development of local firecracker and fireworks factories. In the past, imported firecrackers and fireworks have never caused any danger. Only local factories have had several explosions due to improper mixing of green salt and chlorate. It is found that sounding firecrackers were previously made with a mixture of saltpeter. However, because the use of this raw material, if not precisely matched and tightly sealed, the sound of burning is often not loud. Therefore, in the future, calcium chloride Calcium Chlorate is used for matching, which is louder and easier to manufacture, but there is often a danger of explosion during matching. The local government issued an order on March 1, 1929 to prohibit it. Local manufacturers could not use Calcium Chlorate Calcium Chlorate for manufacturing. The sound of their products could not compete with imported goods. Therefore, the regulations also prohibit the import of firecrackers and fireworks containing calcium chloride. Those who are allowed to be imported in the regulations are all those that local factories have been able to manufacture effectively, so that the local products and imported goods will not be too different.

Permission to Set Off Firecrackers 135

In addition to purchasing for renewal and paying fees in accordance with the law, there is not much relationship with Chinese and European residents. The government pays special attention to the indigenous people. Most of the dwellings of the indigenous people are thatched huts. It is not without danger to set off firecrackers and fireworks at will. In addition, most of the indigenous people have no budget for economy and have no sense of restraint. Whenever there is a New Year's festival, wedding, or circumcision ceremony, they are proud of setting off fireworks and firecrackers. Often, because the consumption is too large, they are unable to pay the national tax. Setting off firecrackers and fireworks must be approved before the government can easily monitor their economic capacity and restrict them.

Firecracker Import Procedures 136

Because the provisions of the regulations, its approval or disapproval, depends entirely on the matching and composition of the raw materials, it is necessary to first submit the samples to the Bandung Firecracker Fireworks Inspection Bureau for chemical inspection to be qualified before paying taxes for import. Otherwise, it will be rejected. In order to avoid this difficulty, exporters should first ask the local Dutch consul to inspect the samples before the goods are shipped, or send them to our country's resident consul or resident consul-general in Jakarta for transfer to the Bandung Firecracker Fireworks Inspection Bureau for inspection. After knowing that it is qualified, it is appropriate to ship it out.

Important Points Regarding Transportation and Sales 137

(1) Article 1 of the Detailed Implementation Rules of the 1932 Ordinance on Firecrackers and Fireworks, Clause (A), Section (Sub-Section): The explosive materials (prohibited raw materials) designated in the laws and regulations promulgated by the Dutch East Indies government in 1893 and amended in 1931 refer to mixtures of the following raw materials: explosive medicines containing gasified substances, picrate salts, blasting powder (green acid), violent explosives, dynamite made with a combination of nitric acid and glycerin, nitro-glycerin and other nitro compounds, Verian explosives, ammonium nitrate explosives (such as

plastic explosives and luminescent explosives, etc.), blasting gelatin, water gel explosives, special explosives, and explosive materials with the same properties as those listed above. Gunpowder made with a combination of niter, sulfur, charcoal, and ink is also included. (Note: Materials without graphite and hard lumps are not included in the prohibition list.) (2) Although calcium gas acid and picrate salts are included in the category of explosive materials, they are indispensable raw materials for the manufacture of fireworks. For example, [Bengal] fireworks, illuminating projectiles, and various other fireworks all use gas acid salts as the main component. The sharp sound effects of rockets, whistles, and cannons cannot be achieved without picrate salts as the main component. Therefore, those who use these materials, if their purpose is not explosion but solely for their light-emitting properties, are not included in the prohibition list. (The sharp sound mentioned in this section does not refer to the explosive sound of firecrackers.) (3) The raw materials mentioned in Clause (B) of Article 1 of the detailed rules are permitted because they are not easily ignited or exploded by vibration or friction. The method used here to check explosive power is to grind the medicinal materials from firecrackers and fireworks between a magnetic pestle and mortar. If they are easily ignited or exploded, they are immediately prohibited. The mortar used has a diameter of 7 centimeters and no glaze inside, while the pestle is 10 centimeters long and also has no glaze on the end that touches the mortar. During manufacturing, one can first test it oneself according to the law. (4) For already manufactured

firecrackers and fireworks, if you want to transport and sell them to the Dutch East Indies, it is advisable to first send samples to the Bandung Firecracker and Fireworks Inspection Bureau for inspection before shipping them, to avoid

complications. It is best to consult with the nearest Dutch consulate regarding the shipment of samples. (Attached is a request form and its translation). Regarding packaging, etc., you should first carefully review the ordinance and its detailed rules.

Ordinance on Firecrackers and Fireworks 138

Translated by the Consulate in Makassar as follows: (1) The amount of dangerous firecrackers and fireworks displayed in front of a store (not in whole boxes) shall not exceed 25 kilograms, and other firecrackers and fireworks shall not exceed 100 kilograms. (A) Clause (Note: Dangerous firecrackers and fireworks are detailed in Article 1(A) of the Ordinance.) (2) In a safe location away from crowds, the total amount of stored firecrackers and fireworks in boxes (sealed boxes) shall not exceed 250 kilograms for those with dangerous properties, and 1,000 kilograms for other firecrackers and fireworks. (Note: According to the provisions of Article 8 of the Detailed Rules, when the quantity of firecrackers and fireworks exceeds 250 kilograms and 1,000 kilograms, they should be stored in specially built warehouses. Refer to the original text of the article.) (3) When packing firecrackers and fireworks, a space wide enough to walk through should be left between each box. The markings on the box surface should all face outward, so that they can be easily seen without moving them during inspection. (Note: Pay attention to the full text of Article 7 of the Detailed Rules.) (4) No easily flammable goods should be stored at the same location as firecrackers and fireworks. (5) The delivery and transportation procedures for firecrackers and fireworks should be handled in accordance with the provisions of Article 7 of Decree No. 10 of the 1933 Government Gazette. (Note: i.e., Article 7 of the Detailed Implementation Rules). (6) If the permit is declared revoked, all firecrackers and fireworks must be handed over within 14 days. (Note: Pay attention to Article 12 and the attached article of Article 12 of the Ordinance, and Article 10 of the Detailed Rules.) (7) All laws and regulations related to safety issues for this type of

business shall apply. (Note: For example, warning signs in Chinese and Western languages should be hung where firecrackers and fireworks are stored, such as [No Admittance for Unauthorized Persons] [No Smoking], etc. It is also advisable not to use oil lamps or candles indoors, and it would be even better to have fire extinguishers available.) (8) When the permit is declared revoked or becomes invalid according to law, the original permit should be returned within 30 days from the date of issuance of the notification. (Note: Pay attention to Article 4 of the Detailed Rules and Article 7 of the Ordinance. If you disagree with the reasons stated in the approval order, you can file an appeal according to the provisions of Article 11 of the Detailed Rules.) This case has been recorded and sent to the Municipal Council, the local administrative chief, the police chief, the fire brigade captain, the director of the Public Works Department of this office, the inspector, the treasurer, and the accountant for their records, and an abstract has been copied and issued to the requester for their retention.

The Bureau of Railways Announces: Director Huang's Sick Leave is a Fact; Returning to Shanghai at the Beginning of Next Month to Resume Duty 139

The Bureau of Railways announced yesterday that Director Huang has taken sick leave due to soreness in his right arm. Rumors that his illness is serious or due to other reasons are all speculation. Director Huang, due to the restoration of the North Shanghai Railway Station and receiving guests for visits in September of last year, felt overworked, which caused the recurrence of his old diabetes. His right arm and

head became sore and painful, making movement difficult. Although various methods such as electrotherapy and massage were used for treatment, they were not very effective. Furthermore, due to heavy official duties, he was unable to rest adequately. Recently, he was persuaded by doctors to decide to take sick leave, which was approved by the ministry. On the 21st of this month, he left Shanghai for Hangzhou and then went to Mogan Mountain for a short stay. Director Huang's diabetes is now gradually improving, and the soreness in his right arm is also gradually decreasing. The news of his serious illness is completely unfounded, and there are no other reasons for this leave besides recuperation. The leave will be at least two weeks and at most three weeks, so he will

return to Shanghai at the beginning of next month to resume duty.

China Merchants Bureau Ordered to Downsize; Preparing to Lay Off Staff and Economize on Expenses 140

Yesterday, General Manager Liu Hongsheng issued a notice and distributed a staff survey form to various departments, stating in brief that the Bureau had been ordered to implement austerity measures. The staff of each department are to fill in their names, positions, dates of entry into the Bureau, salary amounts, etc., as listed in the form. There is also a remarks column, which is to be filled in by the heads of each department with additional comments, stating each person's diligence, laziness, and the complexity of their work, etc., to be submitted to the General Manager by Friday afternoon of this week for assessment. The staff, upon hearing the news, have become very panicked.

Those who deliberately violate this will be severely punished. This notice is issued on the [Day] of April in the 23rd year of the Republic of China. Tao Baichuan, Head of the Department.

Attachment: Continued petition requesting prompt handling. The undersigned merchants previously learned that Fu Zhiqing, the manager of the Oriental Ice Factory, colluded with Gu Fuxiang and others from the Weixing Company, the scum of the machine ice dealers, to organize the Xiecheng Company on Hambi Li Road, monopolizing the products of the Shanghai Chinese ice factories and completing a trust, hoping to manipulate it freely. On April 19, we jointly appealed to your Association (Government) (Bureau) to thoroughly investigate and stop this. Now, the Chinese ice factories have unfortunately fallen into their trap. The compromise method is for people from Xiecheng to use their personal names to subsidize Qiaolong Ice Factory 10,000 yuan per year and Guangyi Ice Factory 5,280 yuan,

in exchange for ceasing operations. In addition, contracts were signed with seven factories, including Dahua, Qiahe, Maochang, Hongchang, Yongxin, and Xin Xie Mao, to exclusively sell at the lowest price permanently, and not to sell to others. For this reason, the price of ice has suddenly increased from about 10 yuan per ton to 17 yuan in the past few days. In the future, we don't know to what extent it will increase. A good market has been ruined by a few scum, which is very regrettable. And the few scum of machine ice dealers are still unrepentant, and dare to hold a big meeting to reverse the facts, and on April 23, they published a news item in the local news column of the Shen Bao, "[Managers of Ice Factories and Fellow Traders Held a Meeting Yesterday to Rectify Trade Rules]," hoping to deceive the society. Qian Acai is the owner of a fruit shop, completely an outsider. How can he participate in the rectification? This is their attempt to deceive the society, and it should be corrected. (2) Fu Zhiqing, who is currently organizing Xiecheng at the Oriental Ice Factory, is the manager of Oriental. How can he be said to have nothing to do with it? This is their attempt to cover up, and it should be corrected. (3) As for the saying that the price of machine ice has fallen and the capital is at stake, it is not true. Because the market price has not changed significantly in the past few decades. Based on the cost over the years, it is at most three or four yuan per ton, while the selling price has been around seven or eight yuan. How can it be said to be losing money? This is their obvious forgery, and it should be corrected. (4) The total number of machine ice dealers in Shanghai is five or six hundred. If they are allowed to hold a big meeting with only six or seven people to organize a joint office, and even want to organize a guild, it is not only a joke, but what else could it be but being commanded by the Japanese? This is their absurdity, and it should be corrected. (5) Furthermore, regarding the engagement of legal counsel, the facts are there, and cannot be concealed by legal counsel. This is their intimidation, and it should be corrected. In summary, the facts are all there, and cannot be reversed. At this time, when the whole country is vigorously promoting the New Life Movement and striving to strengthen the national power, Gu Fuxiang and the Oriental Ice Factory dare to destroy it arbitrarily and risk being unrighteous. It is very hateful. Therefore, a copy of a Shen Bao news item, as well as a list of the number of people organizing Xiecheng Company and a statistical table of all Chinese and foreign ice factories in Shanghai, are attached, and we continue to submit them to your Association (Government) (Bureau) for review and prompt handling, which is for the public convenience.

Yang Bingxun vs. Cai Zhaolu Lawsuit Judgment 144

Yang Bingxun, the inventor of Chinese shorthand, was sued by his disciple Cai Zhaolu from Dongtai, to the Hui Sili (Mixed Court) for biting his ear. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhan Liangce of the First Special Court continued the trial in the Fifth Criminal Court. According to Yang Bingxun, after the previous postponement, he had once contacted to reach a settlement, but it failed because the plaintiff demanded 1,000 gold, etc. The court then advised both parties to make concessions, as they were teacher and student, but the plaintiff insisted that 2,000 gold was the minimum, so mediation was impossible. The trial then proceeded. Cai Guanglu's testimony was the same as before, while Yang Bingxun testified that at the time, he was brutally beaten by the plaintiff and his brother Zhaozheng, and his wife Ni, and his head was dizzy, so he did not know how the plaintiff's ear was injured. He also presented the carter Wang A'er and the maid Zhu Xiaoshi as witnesses. Wang and Zhu testified that they saw the defendant being beaten by the plaintiff and shouting for help. The investigator handling the case then presented evidence proving the investigation situation, and it was seen that the defendant's door had indeed been broken. Finally, Jiang Baolian, the lawyer for the police station, argued that based on the testimonies of both parties and the witnesses, it could be determined that the plaintiff went to the defendant's room to beat him, but although the defendant denied biting the plaintiff's ear, it was obvious that the defendant may have bitten the plaintiff in self-defense at the time. As for whether the self-

defense was excessive, the court should consider it, etc. After the defendant's lawyers Yan Luqing and Da Yaoxian made their defenses one after another, Judge Zhan declared in court that Yang Bingxun was guilty of harming another person's body and was fined 100 yuan. If he chooses to serve time instead, one yuan will be equivalent to one day. Yang indicated that he would consider whether to appeal. The court then ordered a bail of 200 yuan during the appeal period.

it is generally believed that the ginseng market will be completely manipulated by the Japanese in a few years.

Shanghai Prepares for Epidemic Prevention Conference Yesterday - Director of the National Health Administration, Liu Ruiheng, Arrives in Shanghai to Participate - Nine Measures for Cholera Prevention are Resolved 151

Every summer, cholera tends to spread in this city, causing great harm. In view of this, the central health authorities and the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, in the early summer of previous years, joined forces with the health departments of the concessions to organize a joint epidemic prevention agency to prevent and control cholera, with considerable success. As the end of spring is approaching again, in order to make proper arrangements in advance to curb the occurrence of cholera, the Director of the National Health Administration, Liu Ruiheng, specially took the night train to Shanghai on the night before last (the 23rd). Yesterday morning at 10 a.m., he convened the first meeting in the Municipal Government Conference Room to discuss the preparatory matters for prevention. Those present included Liu Ruiheng, Li Ting'an, Fu Qing, Wu Changyao, and representatives of the Public Concession, the French Concession, and the Municipal Council, 14 people in total. Director Liu presided over the meeting, and the following matters were resolved: (1) The terms of office of the members of the Epidemic Committee and the Propaganda Committee are extended for one year. Wu Liande will remain the chairman of the Epidemic Committee, and Li Ting'an will remain the chairman of the Propaganda Committee. (2) In order to save time and money, all stool samples from patients outside the Public Concession but not in the Chinese area must be sent to the Public Concession Municipal Council Laboratory for testing. (3) Epidemic prevention propaganda should focus on areas where epidemics occur and should be intensified. The Propaganda Committee will determine the specific methods. (4) The Epidemic Committee will determine the detailed methods for citizen epidemic prevention inoculation. (5) The next meeting should be held after the end of the epidemic prevention effort. (6) The French Concession should open a Red Cross hospital to accommodate cholera patients. (7) In addition to the existing hospitals, the Municipal Infectious Disease Hospital and the Xizang Road Hospital are designated to admit cholera patients. (8) Food stores and vendors must be strictly inspected. (9) Inform the Public Concession and Chinese area water companies to provide free drinking water to the poor during the summer. Meeting, all members paid a visit to Mayor Wu for a photograph.

After Guo Zibin's Death, His Four Sons Sue Their Stepmother - Accusing Her of Embezzling Property - Initial Trial Lost, Now Appealing 152

Guo Zibin, a wealthy Chaozhou merchant residing in Wenheli, Dagu Road, had assets of no less than ten million yuan. He had five sons. In the fifteenth year of the Republic, Zibin, due to his old age, divided his property and made a will. When Zibin died the year before last, his sons heard the news and rushed to Shanghai to attend the funeral. When they wore filial attire, they saw a mourning couplet hanging in front of their father's spirit, which was sent by their stepmother, Fang. Fang paid someone to write the couplet, but the tone of the couplet insulted the sons. The sons were displeased, believing that their stepmother, Fang, had deliberately insulted them. Therefore, the eldest son, Huatang, removed and collected the couplet. Later, Huatang and his four brothers decided that if their stepmother ever infringed on their reputation or property, they would jointly negotiate with her. All rights and obligations should be jointly responsible, and contracts should be sold and sealed as proof. Subsequently, Huatang and others found that their father had 14,000 taels of silver deposited in the Fuyuan Qianzhuang in Japan, under the name of San Linshi. There were also 18 shares of the Hongyu Yarn Factory on Maigen Road, with a capital of 10,000 yuan per share. In the seventeenth year of the Republic, due to losses, the factory was sold to the Wing On Company. All shares were valued at 2,500 yuan per share, totaling 45,000 yuan. All of the above funds were collected by the stepmother, Fang, and should be handed over and distributed proportionally. It was also found that in the nineteenth year of the Republic, their father had asked lawyer Yuan Hanyun to revise his will in Japan. This will was also hidden by Fang and refused to be handed over. Therefore, they hired lawyer Wu Kaisheng to file a lawsuit against their stepmother, Fang, in court. However, the trial resulted in a loss. Huatang and his four brothers all expressed their dissatisfaction, and

further found that their father Zibin also had two pawnshops, Renyuan Pawnshop and Baoxing Pawnshop, with a total deposit of 1,400 yuan, which had recently been privately transferred by the stepmother, Fang, to the name of her son, Wenzhong. Evidence has already been found, and this point proves that the above two facts have been undoubtedly embezzled. Therefore, they still entrusted lawyer Wu to file an appeal, and the court will soon open for trial. It is also heard that the funeral expenses after Zibin's death amounted to as much as 100,000

yuan, which was used to sell 108 shares of HSBC Bank shares that Zibin had allocated in Japan for charity, and entrusted

a certain qianzhuang to handle the sale, the proceeds of which were used. It can be said that it was the most extravagant funeral in Shanghai in recent years.

Water Patrol Team Patrols the River - Firearms Discovered on the Bank - Wooden Box Filled with Firearms - Shipped from the Taikoo Wharf 153

At around 3 p.m. yesterday, police officers Chen Zhirong and Xin Maosong of the Municipal Public Security Bureau's water patrol team were patrolling the river on a patrol boat when they suddenly saw a sampan with license number 793

coming from east to west near the Taikoo Wharf. They saw that the boat was carrying two passengers and a large wooden box. However, when the two passengers saw the patrol boat parked in front of them, they suddenly looked flustered and restless, which aroused the suspicions of Officer Chen and others. They immediately stepped forward to block their path and ordered them to stop. After boarding the sampan, they carried out an inspection. Because the large wooden box on the boat was very heavy, they used their bayonets to pry open the box lid. After careful inspection, they discovered that the box secretly contained 13 rifles, 10 revolvers, 1,010 rifle bullets, 670 revolver bullets, 9 leather gun holsters, 4 ammunition boxes, 5 leather belts, and a canvas cover, worth approximately

several thousand yuan. They immediately escorted the two passengers who were transporting the wooden box, along

with the boatman, Zhou Xiaoluozi, a Shandong native, back to the team. When Chief Zhu and Deputy Chief Li conducted a preliminary interrogation of the case, one of them, Huang Achang, 43 years old, a Guangdong native, confessed that he was a worker in the storeroom of the British Taikoo Company in Pudong. These firearms were ordered by Cai Qijie, the Chinese bookkeeper in the storeroom, to be transported to the office of the Taikoo Company in Puxi and handed over to a Westerner named Shige (translation). As for whether they were being sold or if there were other circumstances, he did not know. The other passenger, Lu Yaoming, 40 years old, from the same hometown as Huang, and Huang's partner, confessed that he was helping Huang Achang transport the wooden box this time, and did not know the other circumstances. The boatman, Zhou Xiaoluozi, confessed that he was 21 years old and had been hired by Huang and others to transport the wooden box to Puxi, but he did not know that the box contained so many guns. Because the incident involved the smuggling of a large number of firearms, they immediately wrote a report and sent the arrested witnesses to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation at around 6 p.m. last night.

Porters Should Maintain Order When Passenger Trains Arrive - Traffic Department Circulates Letters to All Stations for Compliance 156

The Traffic Department of the Two Roads Administration issued a letter to all stations yesterday, stating, "It has been found that porters at each station still swarm onto passenger trains and compete to carry luggage when passenger trains arrive. This not only disrupts the order of our railway, but also hinders passengers from getting off the train. Moreover, mistakes are easily made or items are lost in the rush, leading to criticism from the outside world. This department has repeatedly strictly prohibited this, and it should be strictly enforced. In the future, when passenger trains arrive, porters should line up in an orderly manner on the platform about two meters away from the passenger train. They must not rush onto the train unless called by passengers. Each stationmaster should be fully responsible

for handling this matter. If there are any violations of this regulation, they should be reported immediately for severe punishment. Do not conceal or neglect them, lest you fail in your duties. In addition to distributing this document, the traffic section chiefs of each section should forward it to all for compliance."

Update on the Water Cut-Off in Peideli - Requesting Fairness from All Organizations 157

The Guowen News Agency reports that Peideli, Dazha Road, Xinzha, was cut off from water at 10 a.m. on the 24th because the landlord, the Catholic Church, failed to collect additional water fees. The houses in Peideli total more than 100 buildings, and the tenants number about 3,000. Drinking water is indispensable, and once it is cut off, they suffer greatly. All the residents held an emergency meeting the night before last and immediately sent more than one male and female representative to the Xinzha Police Station to report the water cut-off situation and request an emergency stop. The police station used the telephone to inquire with the Water Company, and the Water Company sent Chinese and Western officials to the police station to explain. They said that the Catholic Church had sent a letter to the Donation Bureau of the Municipal Council, and then the Donation Bureau ordered the company to cut off the water. If there is a reason, you can negotiate with the Donation Bureau. However, yesterday morning, the tenant representatives negotiated with the Donation Bureau of the Municipal Council, and the reply was that there was no such thing. It can be seen that it is actually a pretext of the Water Company. Yesterday, various alleys in the neighborhood posted many slogans such as "Illegal water cut-off, inhumane" and "Respectfully request assistance from all walks of life," and satirical pictures. On the one hand, lawyer Wang Hangu has been hired as a legal advisor to send a letter to the Catholic Church on behalf of the tenants, giving a serious warning. A letter was also sent to the French Consulate, the Chinese Ratepayers' Association, and the Shanghai Rent Reduction Committee, requesting fairness and providing immediate assistance. It is also heard that yesterday afternoon at around 4 p.m., most of the women in the neighborhood intended to rush into the Qiude Girls' School run by the Catholic Church to fetch water. suffered from fever and chills on February 22nd. The next day, he invited Dr. Ke Shengcang, a Chinese medicine practitioner from Ningbo, to diagnose him at No. 30 Xianggli, East Xihua Road. He believed that it was a case of injured tendons due to a fall and prescribed a prescription containing the medicine of raw soap beans. However, after Feng Xiangguang took the medicine, his whole body ached, he had more than ten consecutive diarrheas overnight, his fever increased sharply, and the situation

worsened. He then hired other doctors to treat him, who diagnosed that Dr. Ke had made a medication error. Now, Xiangguang's condition has turned into scarlet fever and he has been sent to an isolation hospital. He has not yet recovered. Feng Heqing then hired lawyers Shen Zongyu and others to file a complaint with the First Special Court, accusing Ke Shengcang of negligent injury. The Special Court has already summoned Ke twice and ordered him to pay a bail of 200 yuan, pending the submission of the prescription to the Shanghai National Medical Association and the Shenzhou Pharmaceutical Association for identification and verification of the facts. This has been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, the date for the continued trial of this case had arrived. Both the plaintiff and the defendant arrived at the court with their respective lawyers. The Shanghai National Medical Association has also sent a reply to the First Special Court. The content mainly concerns the two points inquired by the Special Court: (1) The child is nine years old, of medium build, if due to a fall and injured tendons, resulting in a hard, red, and swollen lump on the inside of the left hip, fever, and constipation, can he take the prescription? (2) If the superficial syndrome of wind and cold has not been relieved, is there a possibility of pneumonia due to the misapplication of the prescription? Regarding the first point, there is

nothing wrong with taking this prescription to relieve the superficial syndrome, disperse blood stasis, relieve pain, and promote bowel movements. Regarding the second point, it does not seem

likely to cause pneumonia. The

corresponding reply was sent. The presiding judge, Deng Fangcun, issued this reply to both parties for

viewing. Because the witness, Dr. Yuan, did not arrive today, and the identification report from the Shenzhou Pharmaceutical Association has not yet been submitted, he briefly interrogated the plaintiff and defendant and ordered a rescheduling for seven days later. The defendant will remain on the original bail.

The postmaster, Mr. Ma, thoroughly checked the bureau's instructions regarding publications registered as newspapers but found no record of the said publication. He even boasted that Zhu Jiahua was his relative, making a great show of his power and acting unreasonably. Postmaster Ma, realizing that Mr. Chen was beyond reason, reported the entire situation to the management bureau, requesting them to negotiate with the research institute to restrain Mr. Chen from abusing his influence and to issue a warning. This is a brief account of the truth. As for the previous report that the Ministry of Communications ordered the Directorate General of Posts to thoroughly investigate the truth, alleging that the postal worker's attitude was arrogant and made people uncomfortable, it is feared that this was due to being deceived by Mr. Chen, or perhaps there were other emotional factors at play, which are unknown to outsiders.

Reading Q&A

How to Collect and Identify International News (2) 174

Yesterday, I gave a general description of the nature of international news and the knowledge that should be possessed to identify international news. Today, I will further describe how to read international news in Chinese newspapers. - Editor

Chinese newspapers have never paid much attention to international news. In the past, only a few major cities along the coast and the Yangtze River had a row or two of international news in their daily newspapers. As for magazines that systematically discussed international affairs, there were even fewer in the past. Now things are a little different. Because China is so greatly affected by the international situation, and more and more people are demanding international knowledge, newspapers and magazines have gradually begun to pay attention to this aspect. In terms of daily newspapers, Shanghai's Shen Bao, Xinwen Bao, and Shishi Xinbao all have a considerable amount of space to publish international news. Other newspapers such as Zhonghua Daily, Min Bao, Shi Bao, Chen Bao, Damei, and the two evening newspapers, Da Wan, also do not neglect the publication of international news, and the materials are relatively rich. In other cities, such as Nanjing's Central Daily (officially run) and China Daily, and Xinjing Daily, they also publish important international news. The Jing Bao and Chen Bao in Beiping, the Dagong Bao and Yishi Bao in Tianjin, and the major daily newspapers in Guangdong, Hong Kong, and Hankou all have an international news column. Although most of the international news in these newspapers is first seen in the Shanghai newspapers, some of them are first seen in Beiping, Tianjin, or Guangzhou. This is because Beiping is still the political center of North China, Tianjin is the hub of international trade in North China, and Guangzhou is the political center of the Southwest. Their exposure to international developments is sometimes direct. Recently, we should also pay attention to the daily newspapers in Nanchang and Jiujiang. Although they are inland newspapers in nature, the amount of international news is very small, but because Nanchang has in fact become the general hub of Chinese politics today, most of the important meetings and important national policies are decided here. In the daily newspapers here, you can sometimes get fragments of international and Chinese news.

Reading international news in Chinese newspapers is very different from reading international news in foreign newspapers. Generally speaking, in foreign countries, the international news published in national newspapers is largely consistent, but in our country, it is completely different. This is because other countries have control over the news industry, newspapers are large in scale, have wide circulation, have strong economic power, have complete means of transportation, and have a large number of talents, and can send special reporters to various important political and economic centers in the world. Chinese newspapers cannot do this at all. Chinese news not only cannot control itself, but on the contrary, foreign news agencies almost control the Chinese news industry, at least in the international news section. Where do Chinese newspapers get their international news from? They rely on foreign news agencies. The most famous foreign news agencies that supply news in China are the British Reuters, the French Havas, the German Transocean, the American United Press, the Japanese News Alliance and Telegraph Communication Company, and the Soviet TASS. Because they all have different political and economic backgrounds, they directly invade the Chinese news industry by means of political and economic power. Naturally, the articles they issue are only to defend their own national policies, and they contradict each other. This is a characteristic of international news in Chinese newspapers. For people who occasionally read international news, they see many contradictory records of the same international event and do not know who to believe, which is a bit confusing. However, people with experience in reading newspapers find it particularly convenient to understand the truth and falsehood of international events.

Naturally, when reading international news, it is necessary to first check the source of the news and understand its political position and background. First of all, pay attention to the news agency that issued the article. It is not necessary for us to explain the positions of the above news agencies in detail. Except for TASS, which has its own background, the others can be said to be imperialist aggressive forces. The difference is that their respective interests are different and they are mutually antagonistic.

Secondly, we should understand the habit of Chinese newspapers in editing international news. Because Chinese newspapers have always adopted a so-called "objectivist" approach to the publication of international news. That is, many different reports on an international event are published in one place. At the same time, small headlines are used, declaring [X's opinion], [X country's attitude], or [X news agency reported it this way]. What the truth is, let the readers compare for themselves. But this often makes people bored, because the same news is described from various aspects, there are always some repetitions. Careless people will naturally just read a part of it and put it aside. However, experts in collecting international issues and careful readers should not be afraid of trouble and must not be satisfied with adopting a certain opinion. This is the most noteworthy point. This is also the most valuable material.

Third, when checking an international news item, do not discard it because it is a fabricated rumor. You may not believe it, but you should treat it as a companion material. Because even if it is a rumor, it itself has news value. Why does country A fabricate such a rumor against country B? What is the role of the rumor? A person who studies international news (if he has the attitude of a scientist) must pursue the root of the rumor. For example, Japan often spreads rumors that the Soviet Union is increasing its troops in the Far East, etc., in order to cover up the ironclad evidence that it has indeed increased its troops in our three northeastern provinces. There are many examples of this kind. (To be continued)

Spring and Autumn

Fragrant Clouds of the Imperial Incense Burner 175

— Original by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, Translated by Qin Shouou

However, no matter how difficult the problem is, there is always a way to solve it. When the driver or his assistant, the fireman or his assistant, and the brakemen—there were six of them in all—needed to eat or sleep, they could all return to the half-car attached to the back of the water truck. While eating, although it was difficult to stand or bend over, they were all very skilled in squatting, and they could squat to eat or drink tea. We often see Chinese laborers who also like to squat at ordinary times.

Then how about sleeping?

No one can sleep standing up! Even those laborers who are accustomed to squatting cannot sleep squatting! As long as the car moves slightly, they will fall down. But don't worry, there is another very clever way! This method is also commonly used by people in the palace. For example, I am absolutely not allowed to sit in front of the Empress Dowager unless she gives me special permission to sit. Even when she is sleeping and it is my turn to serve her, I cannot sit on any chair or stool privately. But I can sit on the floor or lie on the floor—only lacking a comfortable pillow. Because when I sit or lie on the ground, my body is always lower than her old body lying on the bed, so it does not count as a violation of the law.

The laborers on these cars completely imitated our method.

Although they cannot sit or sleep squatting, they can lie on the floor! In this way, they are always lower than the Empress Dowager. The Empress Dowager in her car, either sits on her throne or lies on the bed. The bed is of course much higher than the floor! (20)

Spring and Autumn White River Bridge 176

— Xiong Wan

Bathing in the warm spring sun, I stepped onto this White River Bridge very lightly and comfortably. The breeze blows across the bridge along the river bank, bringing a lot of rapeseed flower fragrance. The river under the bridge flows slowly, reflecting the sunlight and shining brightly. From time to time, a car whizzes across the bridge; several rickshaws lazily drag across; and several people stroll across with a smile. They are all very natural. Whizzing, dragging, strolling. However, am I too nervous? I always feel that this scene is a bit strange: what the breeze brings is not the fragrance of rapeseed flowers, but it seems to be a bit fishy. The flowing river water is somewhat reddish, like blood. This blackened White River Bridge shows its hideous face, just like the face of General Shirakawa, who slaughtered and burned Shanghai two years ago. I was angry, but I was also afraid. I ran down the bridge in a panic and ran back to Wusong. A large wheel drove in from the Huangpu River, and a red round flag fluttered on the boom. I, nothing!

The Nationality of the Mandarin Orange 177

— Egg

Years ago, when I first arrived in Shanghai, I saw what were called "Siamese Mandarin Oranges" displayed on fruit stands, and in the fruit sections of major companies as well.

This type of orange (actually a tangerine) is more common in the South, yet its nationality isn't specified there. However, once it arrives in Shanghai, it becomes Siamese. When did it acquire Siamese citizenship, or is it truly from Siam? And would the climate of Siam even produce this kind of orange? Even the owners of the large fruit stalls are vague about these questions. They simply call it "Siamese Mandarin Orange" because that's what it's always been called.

In reality, this "Siamese Mandarin Orange" isn't from Siam at all. It is a genuine domestic product, like the Butterfly brand is a domestic star, with no counterfeiting involved.

Besides rice being the major export of Siam, pomelos and mangoes also hold considerable importance. Since pomelos are also found in Guangdong and Fujian, their sales in China aren't as good as mangoes. In the Chinese market, Shanghai's mango supply is almost entirely dominated by Siam. While Luzon's "Ivory Mangoes" are also famous, they are rarely seen. Siam certainly has oranges, a type of tropical orange that is greenish-yellow in color, with a thin skin and sour taste, and not particularly outstanding.

The so-called "Siamese Mandarin Oranges" currently sold in Shanghai fruit stalls are actually the "Pepper Tangerines" from Chaozhou. (Editor's note: Mr. Bohong wrote to say they are called "Jiang Tangerines," produced in Chaoyang.) A genuine domestic product, yet everyone stubbornly treats it as a foreign variety, even attracting the attention of thoughtful individuals like Mr. Wei Jing, implicitly calling for a boycott. Truly, before even leaving the country, it's become an alien. If oranges had feelings, they would deeply resent this.

Four Northeast Company Commanders 178

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 28: Coincidental Viewing of the Opera, Foolish Love Found in a Handkerchief; Diligent Inquiries About Illness, Misunderstanding Through a Letter

During the Lunar New Year, two things left the biggest impression on people: one was the sound of firecrackers at night, and the other was the Spring Festival couplets pasted on people's doors. The absence of firecrackers at night filled Gan Jizhi with many emotions. The next morning, while seeing a guest to the front door, he noticed the red paper fluttering on the doorways of houses along Haidian Street, all bearing Spring Festival couplets, and every door tightly shut. Adding to this were two or three children in new clothes passing by, which made him realize that today's atmosphere was indeed different from usual. After a while, Gan Houzhi went to the government office as usual, and Mrs. Gan invited a few neighbors over to play mahjong, leaving only Jizhi alone in the study. He thought to himself, today is a holiday after all, and sitting at home like this is rather boring. Those Spring Festival couplets on the street are a form of folk literature, why not go and investigate them in person? He could then write a short essay and submit it to a newspaper, perhaps earning a few manuscript fees. With this in mind, he forgot his vow from the previous day not to leave the house. He put on his coat, took a pencil and notebook, and headed out onto the street. He looked at twenty or thirty houses, and found that the couplets were mostly old and cliché, but interestingly contradictory. One butcher shop had the couplet: "Peaceful Times, Benevolent Family." A coffin shop had: "The Seats Are Always Full of Guests, The Jug Is Never Empty." A midwife's house even had the small couplet: "One Person Has Celebration, Five Generations Will Initiate." He wasn't sure if the word "initiate" was intentional or a mistake, but the first line, "One Person Has Celebration," was highly inappropriate coming from a midwife. Imagine how many births she attends, and yet only one person has a celebration, wouldn't that be too tragic? (371)

A Record of the Renovation of Guyi Garden 179

— Haiyang Yuyin

The spring night banquet in the peach and plum garden had Li Bai write a preface for it. The completion of the Joyful Rain Pavilion had Su Shi write a record for it. The ancients rejoiced in their experiences and recorded their magnificence, which was well-founded. Guyi Garden was founded during the late Ming Dynasty, and through the Qing Dynasty to the present, it has been over four hundred years. It has been repeatedly ravaged by war and repeatedly renovated. In the founding years of the Republic of China, it was renovated and refreshed by predecessors and various businesses in the town. In the year of Jiazi (1924), it was destroyed again. During the January 28th Incident, the Four-Sided Hall became a place for tying horses. The pavilions, towers, corridors, and paths were trampled beyond recognition, with only the Mandarin Duck Hall still barely habitable. Initially, Mr. Wang Quantu suggested establishing a Basic Committee for the Mandarin Duck Hall, fostering their dependence. A simple constitution was drafted, and a dozen people signed their names, simply to preserve the historical site, with no grand ambitions for large-scale renovation. In the autumn month of that year, colleagues celebrated Mr. Lu Jingwen's fiftieth birthday, holding a banquet at the residence of Mr. Li Liangcai, and during the banquet, Mr. Lu proposed raising funds to renovate the garden, contributing one hundred silver dollars from his birthday gift money as an initial contribution. Thereupon, colleagues initiated fundraising, and with the sincere support and generous donations of gentry and businessmen from near and far, the collective effort proved easy. Construction began gradually on the twenty-second day of the second month of Guiyou (1933), and was completed by the end of the year after ten months. During this period, workers were hired, materials were procured, walls were decorated, paths were cleared, and flowers and trees were replanted. Suddenly, magnificent buildings stood in rows, shining brightly, and from afar, the trees appeared lush and the atmosphere was magnificent. The desolate scene of the past has been transformed in a short time, and now the gates are crowded with carriages and tourists like clouds. The construction of a large building cannot be supported by a single piece of wood; the reconstruction of an ancient garden cannot be accomplished suddenly by the efforts of one person. As the poem says, "Planning and building it, it will be completed in a short time." If not for the enthusiasm and dedication of the gentlemen involved, how could this have been achieved? As the saying goes, "Where there's a will, there's a way," and now it has indeed come true. I, being unworthy, am fortunate to be a part of this, joyfully witnessing its completion, and humbly write this record.

Poems from the Xuan Yin Lodge 180

— Fu Gong

An ancient intention paints flying rafters, charcoal forming heaps. How many times has a fragrant heart and noble spirit turned to ashes? Bitterly shedding tears of a flowery age like embroidered zithers. Lost in intoxication, the beauty cannot be called back. Imitating the style of Geng Bai, I invite you to join in composing: The red flower beside her temples sways even more gently. The maiden's life is free from all worries. Lightly applying Parisian powder to her cheeks. Wearing clothes that flatter her figure, bearing the brand's seal. Her subtle words reveal she understands from the start. Her passionate emotions pour out like a waterfall, hard to contain. Three years of missteps become a hollow dream. This night urges one's hair to turn completely white.

Random Chat

Research on Inkstones (A Summary of Thirty-One Studies) 181

— Wuliao Ke

The ancients' research on inkstones can be described as meticulous in every detail. For example, regarding the use of inkstones, fresh ink should not be heavily ground, and boiling water should not be occasionally used; hence, there is the so-called "Method of Using Inkstones." Regarding the cleaning of inkstones, heavy stains should be rubbed with floating charcoal, and ordinary cleaning should use lotus seed pods and soap beans; hence, there is the so-called "Method of Cleaning Inkstones." Furthermore, what materials are suitable for making inkstones, and what materials are suitable for lining them; hence, there is the so-called "Method of Storing Inkstones." Regarding the use of inkstones in winter, how to prevent damage and how to prevent freezing; hence, there is the so-called "Method of Warming Inkstones." Regarding repairing damages, how to utilize stone powder and how to forge wax; hence, there is the so-called "Method of Repairing Inkstones." All of these aspects indeed have some artistic flavor, but they are too trivial, so they will be briefly omitted. However, the most relevant point in terms of culture and art is the ability to distinguish between genuine and fake works, which must be studied in detail. As for how to study and distinguish between genuine and fake, the Japanese have a method that can be introduced to everyone.

The Japanese say: It is very difficult to judge the authenticity of poems, inscriptions, and colophons carved on ancient Chinese inkstones. If we want to study ancient Chinese inkstones, we must put effort into ancient calligraphy, painting, and epigraphy. Fortunately, China has recently begun to openly study calligraphy and painting, so we can carefully examine the authentic works of calligraphy and painting to compare and verify the authenticity of the inkstones. For example, if Gao Fenghan carved inscriptions with his left hand, then we must pay attention to whether the calligraphy attributed to him has the same structure and posture. Huang Xintian's carved inscriptions truly have a characteristic Fujian style, and only by seeing more works by Huang and other Fujian artists can we recognize their strengths and weaknesses. Jin Dongxin's style of calligraphy and painting is a variation, and variations are easily imitated, so we must first know the depth of his academic ability and the source of his brushwork before we can gradually distinguish between genuine and fake. Also, for works by Gao Fenghan, Ji Xiaolan, and others that have rubbings, we should study them carefully from the rubbings. There are some famous people who are skilled in calligraphy but not in seal carving, so they hire famous seal carvers to carve seals on their behalf. In this case, it is very difficult to discern whether the original state has been preserved. The Yuan Qifeng Inkstone (Mi Fu's legacy inkstone) collected by Emperor Qianlong was inscribed in his own hand and carved by a famous seal carver, and it is valuable because it was able to maintain its original spirit. In short, to study authenticity, we must widely collect all kinds of inscriptions, clerical scripts, stele inscriptions, and other epigraphic writings, as well as authentic calligraphy and paintings, and diligently look at, compare, and study them every day, without being tired of it. Naturally, we will be resourceful and our knowledge will increase day by day.

Here, I must declare: I introduce this method not to genuinely encourage people to use this method to study ancient inkstones. I only believe that no matter what kind of literature, art, or science is studied, one must start with this foolish and laborious approach. The Japanese are able to use this foolish and laborious approach! Therefore, their country has made such progress. China has many clever people who know immediately upon seeing and understand immediately upon hearing, but they are unwilling to bury themselves in learning foolish methods and putting in laborious effort, so they ultimately achieve nothing. If they continue to rely on their cleverness and are unwilling to start with foolish methods and laborious effort, not only will new culture and new science ultimately lag behind others, with no day of development, but also the few remaining inherent and incomplete learning arts will be abandoned, and in the future, to know something about ancient learning arts, we will have to make a living from the Japanese. What a heartbreaking thing this is! Pointless talk about inkstones is originally for leisure and amusement and has no great relationship with literature and art. It is up to you whether you read it or not, whether you study it or not. However, this last sentence, I hope everyone must remember it firmly, only then this article will have some small meaning.

Sun Che, Our Country's 10,000-Meter Athlete Participating in the Far Eastern Games, Died Suddenly Yesterday Morning; Suffering From Both Pneumonia and Liver Disease, He Died in the Red Cross Hospital; He Once Set a New National Record of 34 Minutes and 1 Second in the 10,000 Meters 183

Sun Che of Shanxi Province, our country's 10,000-meter athlete participating in the Far Eastern Games, recently sought treatment at the Red Cross Hospital for pneumonia. It was thought that he would recover quickly and win glory for the country. Unexpectedly, the tragic news arrived yesterday. Mr. Sun, suffering from both pneumonia and liver disease, passed away suddenly at 12:30 AM last night (the 24th) before he could be treated. In total, he was only in the hospital for three days. Not only does this mean our country has lost a hope in the Far Eastern Games, but it is also a major loss for the sports community in our country. Alas!

Relapse of Old Illness According to Ma Yuehan, the coach of our country's Far Eastern Games track and field team, according to Mr. Sun himself, he had a history of liver disease, which would recur from time to time,

but he didn't take it seriously. This time, his old illness relapsed. At first, he didn't take it seriously. Then he caught a cold, and his lungs were also affected. The symptoms this time were different from before. He jokingly said to Mr. Ma, "My illness is different, I'm afraid I won't be able to return home." Mr. Ma scolded him for his wild talk and comforted him with kind words. He was immediately sent to the Red Cross Hospital on Hague Road for treatment.

He Died Suddenly The doctors diagnosed him with pneumonia, but at first, they didn't think it was serious. On the second day of his admission, Mr. Ma still thought he would recover soon. Unexpectedly, his condition deteriorated sharply, and both illnesses broke out together, leading to his death. He passed away around 12:00 AM on Sunday night. The tragic news spread quickly, and everyone was shocked and lost color. Yesterday morning, the Association and Mr. Ma took care of all the funeral arrangements and placed the coffin in the Shandong Guild Hall on Wangzhi Road.

When the coffin was being prepared in the hospital, all the Far Eastern Games athletes in Shanghai went to the hospital to pay their respects and express their condolences. Telegram to His Family Mr. Sun belonged to the Second Regiment of the Zhengtai Railway Guard in Shanxi. Yesterday, the Association urgently telegraphed the Shanxi Provincial Department of Education and the Second Regiment of the Railway Guard in Yuxian County, Shanxi, led by Regiment Commander Lang.

His Record Mr. Sun participated in the North China Far Eastern Games preliminary rounds in Tianjin this time. He set a new national record of 34 minutes and 1 second in the 10,000 meters. In the Shanghai preliminary rounds on the 14th of this month, he still achieved a result of 34 minutes and 49 seconds, breaking the national record and winning the championship. Such talent, yet Heaven did not grant him long life. What more can be said?

Youth Association Initiates Billiards Competition Scheduled for May 15th 199

Billiards is a refined form of entertainment, widely enjoyed by many Chinese people. Various competitions are often held. Now, the local Chinese Youth Association will initiate a billiards competition to promote individual skills and increase interest in the game. It is scheduled to be held on May 15th at the association's hall in Baixianqiao. Eligibility is temporarily limited to members of the association. The competition guidelines are listed below:

(1) Purpose: The purpose of this billiards competition is to connect members and promote friendship. (2) Eligibility: All members of the association can register. (3) Registration: Registration is open from now until May 14th. Anyone interested in billiards can register. (4) Time: The competition will start at 5:30 PM daily from May 15th. (5) Quota: This competition is temporarily limited to 40 participants. (6) Fees: Participants are required to pay a registration fee of one yuan, which will be used for a dinner after the competition. (7) Competition Method: After the registration quota is filled, the competition committee will draw lots and adopt an elimination system. (8) Prizes: In addition to commemorative gifts donated by association members to the top three winners, the association will also prepare a special commemorative plaque with the names of the top three winners engraved on it, to be kept at the association for remembrance. (9) Location: Billiards room on the second floor of the Baixianqiao Association Hall. (10) Announcement: The decisions of the judges during the competition will be final.

5,000-Meter Long-Distance Relay Race: Xiguang Overwhelms Datong University, Wu Xiecheng Wins Individual First Place 201

Yesterday afternoon, under bright sunshine and a vibrant spring atmosphere, the 5,000-meter long-distance relay race between the Xiguang cross-country team and Datong University was held as scheduled. Famous Sports Works for Primary and Secondary Schools: Publication of "Standard Exercise Implementation Methods," Essential for Physical Education Teachers in Primary and Secondary Schools 204

The Qin Fen Bookstore at 392 Laoshenfu Road in Shanghai has always been dedicated to publishing sports books and newspapers, contributing new materials to sports, and promoting new sports. The book has been published and is a work of careful study and experience by Mr. Sun, with rich content. The complete table of contents is listed below: Chapter 1: Introduction, Chapter 2: Physical Education Achievement Examination, including two points: Calculation and Examination Methods, and Scoring Standards. Chapter 4: Exercise Standard Testing Scoring, including What is Exercise Standard Testing, How to Apply Exercise Standards, People Who Do Not Meet Standard Testing, Why Ball Games Are Not Standardized, Group Testing, and five points. It also includes Exercise Achievement Score Examination Tables for Each Group, Long Jump Achievement Score Comparison Table, High Jump Achievement Score Comparison Table, Shot Put Achievement Score Comparison Table, Double Arm Curl and Pull-Up Achievement Comparison Table, Athlete Testing Various Exercise Achievement Score Comparison Tables, Ball Games Standard Testing Methods, Miscellaneous Exercise Standard Testing Methods, Chapter 5: Equipment, Chapter 6: Competition, Appendix: Table for Calculating Actual Age from the Old Lunar Calendar. This book is essential reading for primary and secondary school physical education teachers. The price is four dimes per book, with a special price of 10% off. The bookstore's store at 277 Simalu Road is also selling it at the same price.

Education News: Other Locations

Ministry of Education Maintains Local Education Funding: Taxes Used for Education Remain Unchanged Until Firm Compensation Is Provided, Executive Yuan Instructs the Ministry of Education to Order Provinces and Cities to Comply 205

News from the education sector: In order to maintain local education funding, the Ministry of Education submitted a request to the Executive Yuan in February of this year and issued a circular to provincial and municipal governments, stating that taxes used for education funding should strictly comply with the Measures for Guaranteeing Local Education Funding. Until a firm and equivalent compensation is provided, the status quo should be maintained to preserve education. The Executive Yuan believes that abolishing harsh and miscellaneous taxes is an important policy of today, but education is tied to the lifeline of the nation, and guaranteeing education funding is also not to be neglected. Local governments should urgently consider proper compensation for these types of taxes, taking into account both considerations. Therefore, the Executive Yuan issued a circular to provincial and municipal governments to investigate various harsh and miscellaneous taxes and scheduled a meeting in June of this year to plan for the abolition and compensation measures. The intention is none other than to reduce the burden on the people while still preventing major impacts on local affairs. Because the Ministry of Education's request to maintain the Measures for Guaranteeing Local Education Funding is for the sake of planning compensation and is not inappropriate, it has been instructed to the Ministry of Finance to inform them, and the department has issued a special instruction to provincial and municipal governments to handle the matter jointly. It is understood that the department has already issued instructions to education departments and bureaus across the country to instruct their subordinates to comply.
